And the sign of an arrow that never goes into the flesh is when there's no foam spurting from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient has a changed color, and they sigh loudly with a hot forehead.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow has exited through the buttock's cover, it is beneath the small ribs; and produces great pain and sighing; and moves all limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if it's an arrow or stomach, by chance if there is no matter from the meat undigested in the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if it's an arrow or stomach, and in the case of a jump there is no dung passing through the intestines, then there is no hope in treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if it's an arrow or stomach in the bladder, and urine comes out by jumping and leaves, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and chest and neck and shoulder blades and the shoulder joint and the spine of the back and the ribs and the kidneys and the legs, and similar body parts, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in one's nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do that other thing.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at one point where an arrow hit someone in the shoulder blade at the base of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and moved it from that side through the fat behind the ear; there was no significant sensation.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I tested an arrow that fell in the fat near the eye below the paper,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow had been withdrawn, and it could no longer reach even to the tip toward the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as an arrow from Turkey, weighing about one pound without ears; the wound healed properly, and no adverse events occurred to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And shot an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was the Arab type with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I aimed for the necks, and guided it as I shot it, and the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take out an arrow at two inches deep, where it was stuck in the back or belly, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then since it had passed thirty days, if it did not change its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut through the arrow, I tried to pull it out, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you encounter an arrow that fell on or hit someone's back, resulting in a wound that is sealed;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And allows the arrow to remain within, not returning to its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And finds no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And saw one other man who had an arrow wound on his face, and he was joined together the injury;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it felt like this causing a great pain to remain; and many similar things occurred.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And try to extract an arrow from the first half of the body of the king's son, as it was stuck in his chest halfway.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and had slightly moved towards the right side; and the arrow was completely inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for the treatment after it had been three days since it occurred. I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried all sorts of delicate methods and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt a burn and pain around his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed on him a plaster that is absorbent and restorative, because his limbs were swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrow in his limb.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied plaster to the wounds on the days, and resolved the injuries immediately, then let the patients recover for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he felt the arrow within his nose; and I told him this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive aqua regia to the wound by my own hand until it was opened,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tested it, and felt the tip of the arrow which was pointing upwards.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjust during the opening of the wound through this medicine, until I visibly saw the head of the arrow;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and made sure to penetrate deeply inside for about four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then I would loosen the wound so that my fingers could reach it from both sides, and couldn't escape;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I didn't stop refining and devising ways to use tools, until I had taken it out on the second day with well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to how its form will come to an end in the conclusion of this chapter, while I am treating it, and I will heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the judges determine that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will heal it then, and seal the wound, and completely recover the patient.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	You have been told about the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you place your treatment on what I do not say, because the book cannot take everything into consideration;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but trust your wise master brother with some small matter, and regarding what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	trust in nine works, and the ninth tool, for their role in removing foreign bodies that occur in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows penetrate the limbs where they are embedded only according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	by their head where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that leaps in through the wound or where it enters, this is an arrow entering into their flesh, and it now pierces once again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't pierce now, let her grow until the meat is ripe inside, and wait for the discharge;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it's stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let her stay like that for a few days, and remove her each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, if it pierces through all the way to the very end of a slender piece for piercing, as long as there is space inside for the needle, and then guide.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is stuck in the skull bone, and goes until it touches one of the brain chambers,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and all the incidents I have mentioned appear to the patient: if they do not remove it immediately, but leave it until the swelling is equal after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes up to the eye socket, it's death for them.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is fixed only through bone and does not reach up to there,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the patient remains without any bad incident for a few days,
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's firmly placed in such a way and cannot come out at all,
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been restored inside the body so well that it can't be seen,
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, guide it to any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do so by the constriction of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then make incisions as long as the wound becomes larger;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	remove the arrow if you can, and if it has hooks on the arrow that hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If you want to remove a bone that is stuck at two places, use force until you can pull it out.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrow's ears as long as you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Do this carefully so that you do not break the arrow but draw it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't remove it in one go, let the shaft be buried up to its feathers until it's broken, then pull it out, for the extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding is against your wish during this process, apply what we have instructed about treatment in our chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting near nerves and veins, and do it carefully so as to draw out the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or gently, firmly or clumsily; and guide the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it is the greatest help that I be, and if you cannot do so, place him according to what the mark shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it exposes any part of the wound, or if there is swelling in the area where you can see or feel it obviously:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then cut upwards, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then press: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, twist your hand around it as long as it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot come out, leave her still, and then begin the extraction again until she comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if the shaft of the arrow is there, one should push it all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it is in the anus, and you see it needs pressing out, then press it with an instrument having a sharp tip,.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters the channel of the tool; and then force it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is bent, I use another instrument with a point entering inside, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if an arrow has hit you, it is necessary that you cover all the flesh around or at its entry point, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then clean the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits or pierces it in the chest or stomach or bladder or ribs, and is close to vital organs, then if you can cover it, do so;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then stitch up the wound; if that is what requires doing.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until she/he has recovered.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used for arrows resembles an bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	because forcing at the tip of an arrow, as it is shaped thus:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape like that of pincers for pressing and picking so is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common bodies
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From the veins from which we cleanse are thirty-one, from which there are sixteen heads.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This refers to: The two small things behind the ears, which are called the "two herbs";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins which are in the grooves of the two eyes, and they are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is inside the forehead; and the vein that is at the root of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two guide poles which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are in the cheeks above the mouth, and these veins are called 'augueherich'.
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the two veins that are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins of which we commonly speak are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cervical joint, and it's at the left rib area, and they call this 'the vein of the head';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the median one is called 'fast', and it consists of the cervical joint and the basilic vein,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	They call this 'the artery of the heart'; and as for the basilic vein, if it is at the right rib area,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call this condition "the vein of the belly", and it's located on the flank,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that which can be healed, which opens clearly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the artery is the vein located between the index finger and the ring finger, and it's two inches long;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the patella is, there are three veins: one is under the bend of the thigh on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And this second sinew is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "the nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins besides those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps with hangovers and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the surgeon, as I tell you, is that you will laugh at the pain of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the arm or veins with an abrasive cloth; then pinch the patient's throat to their neck.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until the two veins become visible behind the ears in the two arms hanging down from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Then place your hand there, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, let it beat rhythmically;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet and place the needle just below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way above the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and let the skin and the vein well two inches deep through, and make blood come out as long as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then hold and tie it, until the wound heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken about the incision and the fire cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it involves ancient lead poisoning,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And similarly, and with ointment accustomed, and at the body of feverish tears by the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the physician is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And when the patient strains their throat, until the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse on both sides, and then listens for an echo.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the knife over the vein upwards towards your thumb tip, and hold the scalpel steady.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein upwards, and make an incision, just as you did in other veins, and pour out the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient's body, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put a cotton pad there.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form the wound and leave it until it heals; and we have spoken about this and its treatment, as well as its extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as that of the frontal sinus for ancient diseases of the face, and migraines, and fever;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the tool called a 'digger', whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or some other tool, allowing blood to flow out according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck, and bind the vein as long as it is healthy and without any cut or wound. And once an incision has been made with a broad flame,
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always, it is not right that the flames be too fierce and directed from side to side; instead one should use gentle heat, for the bone is close by. By chance, if the flame were sharp, it might break the bones when they are brittle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The treatment of the two veins that are in two eyes helps with the tears, and at the nose, and at the cheeks, and under the eye in the socket, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their treatment is such that patients tighten their neck by twisting around some string, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and make the healing pass through, somewhat long like a flame's width somewhat broad, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle and accidentally break, then make it correspond to the blood flow up until you need to do so, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein near the nose is valuable for an ailment like an ointment application and after the face has been cleansed, and for diseases affecting the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and redness that come to the face, and similarly when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of health is such that the patient narrows their throat, then restricts their nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long subtle flame, and stick it inside the mouth in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well yet, and the blood will now start to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far in this position, and apply blood gently according to your need, then leave it for a night, as it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And it's the shape of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two kidneys aids in tightening the liver, and in the beginning of melding disease, and for many illnesses, and in putrefaction, and corrosion, and in herpes, and tumours;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of this health is that the patient's throat is tightened from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master be on the head of the patient, and the disease sit at one point,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then cleanse the vein as long as a bit more widely, then drain the blood gently, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then make another incision in the other vein, then release the tie, and gently restrain the veins somewhat.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let them not strangle the patient; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	Cleaning of the lungs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of veins above the lips aids in collection within the mouth, and decay of gums, and tears in lips, and nosebleeds and congestion.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing consists in having the patient stand before you, and restraining their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them because they are black, and because inside them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore handle both of them, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt about them,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you handle the largest of each side, and do exactly the same for the two veins that are above and below it, because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the treatment concerning the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of veins that are located in the neck receive help after the treatment of the head vein, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and among eye diseases, and among mouth illnesses;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of a surgeon is that when diseases are squeezed between your hands in front of the sun, and lifted the tongue, and you look at each side there is a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then it's healthy for both, but do not squeeze too much, because there are the arteries nearby.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins in the arm which we commonly treat are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	at every point of .i., ignite a large iron needle, or use a slender olive branch like a sharp knife, and call it "anisel";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide yet fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the iron needle is much celebrated, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it's needed to open hair-filled veins filled with obvious blood, and those containing thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more slender and pointed, and it aids in thin veins or has thin blood of a citron color.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilica's healing quality, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, and neck, and chest, and stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it's proper for the healer to heal gently, and to be aware of the artery that is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he presses on the artery, and blood starts flowing out, should it happen, you need to stop the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be grasped by the flame, but cut with them like a knive.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if it is clear that the basilic vein does not open, then you should try to extract it and use another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Or if you want no part of this, or you decide to replace the vein with your arm: it clearly opens.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cure with fire comes before, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you understand the location of the pulse, it is thus that you should stretch the arm, touching the site until you know the beat.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place for cutting, and then bind the arm, and apply fire to that area before it.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to cut the artery when you see the place swelling, for that is where the artery is: watch out there then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding up as much as the urine of a child, and the sinew is red and subtle, know that this is a sinew from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your finger for a long time, then stabilize your finger so that the wound is sealed, as this has happened many times;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Tie up the arm, and leave it like that, do not move the patient; and be afraid, do not move until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound has not sealed and you need to do something, and the medicine is not at hand, then cut the artery if it opens, because that's how blood flows out; and seal the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of walnut shell, and cut it open, and take one half and bind well up to the other edge;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	leave it uncoated, that's good; if not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the coatings should not be too tight for the small area of the wound and the strength of the connection of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The treatment for a vein injury in the middle is to use the means to stop blood flow from both above and below, and on either side.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is made of the basilica and cephalic parts, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the surgeon to be aware of the location of the nerve that is nearby, and if he does not go too far in, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it swells up and damages health, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any of the bodies due to its subtlety, then you should heal it from the scalpel beforehand; and feel for the nerve with your finger.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two fingers, cut it as long as necessary.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The relief of the forehead helps, when it evacuates blood from the head, and assists with the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to warm with the olive oil flame or the myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because there is neither a nerve nor an artery near it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	All right then, it's necessary to try the lightest weight, and don't be discouraged if it doesn't work the first time, simply try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance swells up some men's ears, cannot it be the first time, but it causes no pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about a surgeon is that surgery is managed solely to maintain health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the healing take place at one of the three veins that are there: this means, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilical;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be treated at the beginning of prayers while kneeling, and in autumn and after meals during winter, when the sign of fullness is seen;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it should be treated on the first or third day, after two days or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The treatment for diseases does not have a fixed time, but it is given whenever the need arises during the day or at night.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not advisable to nurse children until they are twelve years old, nor a pregnant woman only for three-quarters of her month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Neither should anyone over sixty years old be nursed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when one wishes to nurse himself, in any way that might be the case, it is necessary for him to cleanse his intestines with a gentle cathartic,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has retained some dung, so that the veins drain the superfluous fluids out of the main parts causing harm;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	No one heals well who is too full of meats, or who is drunk, as long as they have strength, or are dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And when someone is better after colic pain, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent urination, and excessive bed rest during pregnancy, and work, staying awake and walking, or that which quickly loses its strength, or through something from the arm or injury to the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the body fluids, if it is too full of meats and drinks and medicine, but you have the ability to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then try a bath, if there's no objection, to refine the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And cure of the vein from the lower part up to one-third from inside, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep that day for work, and pain, and excess, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And tie yourself tightly and warmly, and ensure that the bandages are higher than where you're treating, and rub your arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then adjust the bandage moderately above, because if it is too tight or not enough, then you cannot correct the wound;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with hands until the veins swell, and when you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the wick of the lamp with a little old oil, then place your left thumb on that vein under the shoulder a bit where you want to puncture;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not rupture and bleed when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For some veins leak like strings when pricked, while others are full of wind and thus do not leak.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	If indeed when one places upon the flame, it retires to the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens the vein, the wound is too narrow for this reason, so one must be skilled in these matters for the surgeon.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good; if not, try again slightly under or at once near that spot, where the limb is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and there's anxiety in the patient, let it rest for one or two days, don't bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, there may come pus-soaked discharges; do not enter or bathe, then restart the cleansing if it pleases her;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wick is small, or the string is too fine and you doubt whether it passes through as much blood as you see, so pierce that very wick straight across to all the flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and the ointment a little quickly, so that the limbs are swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swells up, do not start cleansing again, instead put a little of animal oil on it, for it helps relieve the body of blood and is effective at this point where the oil lies.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus apply the oil in each healthy part that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And similarly apply garlic and mustard seeds, when you place them on the body; if the oil is too thick it will leak out.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess that is large, which happens often, even when it has not been healed yet only once or twice, especially when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you rush in, soak an sponge with water and a little hot wine and salt, and keep it on the body for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the expulsion of blood from the vein, and if it stays in place after several days without any blackness or verdure, then it does not harm the patient.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see that, place on it some thing of aloes or of myrrh made into a juice of rue, gentian, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance to the healing of the basilica occurred: then place your hand there, and if you find that the area is soft upon pressing with your hand, then this indicates a bad condition.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said to the affected area because you might inadvertently touch an artery; but instead, apply two layers of dry plaster to harden the area, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And lead each one to blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it continue to flow until it thins out; and if it's too thin, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is for the one who is full and stricken, needing blood extraction; you should make him have a larger wound, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make him well, often apply it, and when treating him, cut across, not straight.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	In this method of healing, it saves from the running out of blood and constriction of nerves, and is more effective than a long cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body requires healing, it is necessary to give them a moist paste made from juice of quince apples; if they are hot, let blood flow four or five times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold constitution, eat before healing a moist paste in a syrup flavored with herbs, or an aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and caraway seeds, with a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they have trouble healing after blood has been discharged during treatment, it's good for them to inhale broth of lamb and a subtle-smelling syrup,
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And apply the other things that we have discussed in the chapter or section on collapse, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to strengthen his arm, and improve it again, should it be necessary, when he is weakened by excessive improvement, he should improve slowly and gradually, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wishes to strengthen their arm after the first improvement, and they have robust health, then they should improve for seven hours after the first improvement, or even after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to strengthen themselves on another side, then they should improve the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body that has become heated, and it causes fever; so one must drain a large quantity, and widen the constriction until it flows freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then you ensure all conditions for health, and place your hand on the healthy lungs so that death does not come from suffocation.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	This happens many times when hygiene is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it should not happen when you see the arm coming out and blood escaping for a second time, and if the constriction is closed, then you should press firmly;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it's twisted, stretch out your arm quickly, for that would be ill.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it until the second time it heals; or you light at the tip of the flame, until the frost which was frozen off comes out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on one and a half a pinch of salt that has been boiled in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be alone and don't compress it, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to bleed again, if it can be done in that place itself, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is located on the arm where it overlaps with the head because it's made up of that part.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of bleeding is such that the patient holds their hand in warm water, until the veins become red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then moderately bind it, so that the vein appears clearly, then bleed now through it, neither too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And make sure they are wide, and have them very close to the joint of the hand, if unable to move them, then place the hand in warm water and leave the blood in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is winter, do not warm up your hand with hot water either, because you would rather be in winter than winter.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And this vein's healing is safer compared to all others, there being neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The recovery of the right hand's salvation is valued against all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strengthen your hand, and dip it in hot water, as long as the vein is closed, if you can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it's cut across, and if you press right through with all your force, so that nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too far in the middle, because the nerve is completely bare of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put your hand in hot water, if the flesh is frozen in the wound and can't escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as your skill allows, place over the vein there and seal it to rapidly fuse, and thus do for each case.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of his left hand corresponds to the disease in the mouse, and do everything as I have instructed you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The treatment of the soul corresponds to all diseases that exist within the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the heart, and congestion of fluids, and diseases of veins, and old leg diseases, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its healing is such that the patient should soak in hot water and rub it on the wound until it heals,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot much blood flows.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Heal it then or more widely on the leg, or at the ankle that suits.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the leg, be careful of the nerves which are nearby, and also make your incisions as when sewing; may the flames extinguish themselves.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out without causing injury, immerse the limb in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is a new injury, then for the first time, if you repeat it on the second one slightly above, because the earlobes are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Never doubt a nerve, as we have said, and similarly perform on the other side with equal measure.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic nerve is at the knee of power, and its health matches with pain in the hip, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And its quality of health is that the limbs move or swim, and it twists above the ankle by three inches in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise, the vein does not open; and if it does open, you heal it in every way that you can, and when crossing through;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And move her as you hold her, for the arm is free, and she responds much to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find her, heal none of the veins that open or towards the foot, and be cautious of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make sure to correct any blood flow that you see, and then untie the knot, put on cotton, and tighten it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Extracting with suction devices
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or spiders, or glass; and suction treatment can be performed in two ways: by piercing to draw blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction treatment that involves piercing follows two methods: it can be done with any heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	Suction treatment performed by piercing and blood extraction is carried out during the first twelve days of menstruation,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Because one's head is entirely inside the skull; and the other sticks out from the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two more are in the second ribs beneath the neck; and the beard under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the axilla is between the two shoulders; and the axilla above the elbows.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the pits are under the two arms; and the pits of the legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suction cups of the two ankles; and suction treatment does not involve bloodshed, because it deals with small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And for this reason one does not weaken oneself at all, as is done in treating veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or without it, in any illness that comes from overfullness, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases suction must be applied, or out of habit, then we administer it each hour at the beginning of her period, or at the end, and in between, and at every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they have need to suction, if they hold their head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who find congestion and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and are blind with them;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and for those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongues, and spit out blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who think, see through the nose bleeding and vomiting, and such like things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, indeed even during the month, we instruct to suction after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The treatment of the nose helps in alleviating the fever of the head… that comes from the eyes, and it should not be done after the elimination of all throughout the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this suction is part of the treatment for the headache,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not suitable for those with cold constitution to use them, or who have diarrhea, because this causes much harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And it is not suitable for the old either when using them, nor those with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who frequently uses it becomes forgetful, for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup somewhat further down due to the possibility of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Ligature around the neck is in the place of the health of the head and the basilic vein, for this reason it is effective at constriction below the elbow.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And to cut through the channel of the pericardium, and immediately, and to refill;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is best to gently press, for if you hold too firmly, it may cause constriction or blockage in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The windings on the two ribs under the collarbone can relieve head pains, eye and toothaches, and in stridor, and for pain in the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is at the site of the basilica's healing; and you should instruct the surgeon to place his hand there without pressing on the artery, nor let blood flow repeatedly.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilation of the chin leads to illness in the mouth, and decay of gums, and similar diseases which occur within the mouth; and it is related to the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the shoulders leads to illness that comes from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Ventilation of the elbows is as important as three veins in the arms.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it carries blood from these major veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the warrior not to bend too far forward, for his chest is naked of muscle, and knows underneath skin and veins.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup on the buttocks is suitable for bleeding from the bottom and diseases underneath, it requires that the suction cup be large and made of iron, as it needs to be well treated; if it were too thin by chance, it would break; I make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups operate openly, because they drain blood from the entire body, and are effective for old pain in the kidneys, and the liver, and bladder diseases, and promote menstruation; they are located on the inner knees and ankles, and all over the body; also, after long use, they weaken the body and cause fatigue in various situations.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you should apply it after checking thoroughly and ensuring a continuous sucking action. Apply it quickly, move it evenly, and keep doing this until you see the skin turning red and swelling, then release the suction. Afterwards, put the suction cups back on, take care with how your body is positioned since there are some who have very thin flesh and clear pores: in such cases, one should pierce only once, and make wide cuts but not too deep; apply light suction.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the patient is large, it's appropriate to strike twice: the first time for the purpose of making a small incision for the sake of the thick blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the patient is very dense, it's appropriate to strike three times; and when we wish to drain a little blood at a time, we only need to make an incision once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to take a lot of blood, we repeatedly perform the procedure; and if the patient is dense, strike through deeply, and ensure that the veins are pierced immediately.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is suitable for those with thick and hard skin who have become red from long exposure, that you apply the cups of the suction and dissolving pessaries to their limbs.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it's in this state, from where it bleeds, or from the oil of sweet almonds, or from the seed oil of a cucumber;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it's in sweat, from spinach oil, or from rosemary, or chamomile, or other similar substances.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of wormwood, or of balm, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person being treated has tender flesh and large pores, there should be no oil applied at all.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is advised to wash after the suction of pink water, or cold water, or water from a rose, or water from a cucumber plant, or water from a porcelain vessel, or other similar substances.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have some moisture, if they rise from rest or from water of myrtle and sumac, and other similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And for those who have large excesses, they arise from old wine, or water of succa, or decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not advisable for a bath attendant to use suction cups before or during the bath, but rather after the bath one hour or two hours; and do not sleep after suction treatment,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it must be understood when one should suck and when it has been sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	Guard yourself against the one who is healing and hot-tempered, and if he is too heated and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It's necessary for him to eat cold things, such as apples, radishes, and lettuce on the side, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	Eat young rabbits, pork meat, and damp meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for the one with a cold constitution, if they desire syrup made from honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and small pieces of bread, and fritters and small birds and baby pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day they feel an appetite, they should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give some men neither trialect nor muscat wine before or after the appetite appears, in order to strengthen their main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And season the broth with spices, but it is not good for those who are hot to drink them.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed to cause irritation are those placed on the liver, and on the lungs, and in gout, and on the stomach and intestines and kidneys and hip, because this limb does not suffer from being pierced by needles.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from member to member,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	just like we place them on the nipples when a person is bleeding; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just like we place suction cups on the stomach and intestines to reduce the size of the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, just like it happens by its attractive power to some extent with the obstruction, or empties the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And then perform it when you place it over the heart and under the lungs, where there is a retained gust of wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these suction cups are administered empty only for sucking; and they are never used together with fire, and they are not filled with water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	just as in diseases caused by colic, and in such a manner that we fill the suction cup with hot water, or with water where herbs useful for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used over fire is like this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two sticks half the palm wide and at both sides of the middle one small notch each way as to place a needle in,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be made of iron, so that when you place it on the limb, it does not harm the patient;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a rod across from an eel or iron, to put a candle in.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and they are thinner than those of fat individuals.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And thus should one place this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take a wax candle or a single line, and insert it through the suction cup which is in the suction cup, across the penis which is in the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup and it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the limb, and you must either on the spot that we have mentioned, so when one wishes, if it goes there steam, and removes it with the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And apply the dressing in the same way as before, and repeat often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup, which is administered in pleurisy disease, during all fevers, there should be neither a penis nor any part of it, and it is only administered when it is full of water, and placed only on the limb.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without ears are treated only on limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the treatment of burns on them, such as cheeks or nose, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And when you find ears that are in fresh water without infection, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water until they become familiarized and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then cleanse with vein opening and suction, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place on bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full, and bleed, if it is possible to place suction cups there, do so, for this is of little value afterwards.
